Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





While having finished typing into a web site form open in Chrome and moving the pointer away with the touchpad, a small popup window appeared notifying: The document "FILENAME.jnlp" could not be opened. GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent cannot open files in the "Java web start" format. That FILENAME.jnlp is located in my user Download folder and was downloaded a few weeks ago for a test. It is buried behind several hundred other downloaded files and as I have sorted my Download folder by latest added time, it is not visible automatically. That means either a) something unknown in the background must have launched GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent with FILENAME.jnlp as parameter or b) GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent has decided on its own to open it. See attached screenshot of that popup window.



<span class="line"><!---->While having finished typing into a web site form open in Chrome and moving the pointer away with the touchpad, a small popup window appeared notifying: The document "FILENAME.jnlp" could not be opened. GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent cannot open files in the "Java web start" format. That FILENAME.jnlp is located in my user Download folder and was downloaded a few weeks ago for a test. It is buried behind several hundred other downloaded files and as I have sorted my Download folder by latest added time, it is not visible automatically. That means either a) something unknown in the background must have launched GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent with FILENAME.jnlp as parameter or b) GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent has decided on its own to open it. See attached screenshot of that popup window.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Both scenarios should not be possible to happen as a) appears to be only possible if GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent is started with sudo as otherwise it will fail to start completely and I have definitely not launched anything manually with sudo at that moment and never accessed GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent even before. I have SophosEndPoint from my employer running since several months and never had malware on any of my Macs.



<span class="line"><!---->Both scenarios should not be possible to happen as a) appears to be only possible if GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent is started with sudo as otherwise it will fail to start completely and I have definitely not launched anything manually with sudo at that moment and never accessed GoogleSoftwareUpdateAgent even before. I have SophosEndPoint from my employer running since several months and never had malware on any of my Macs.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;

           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */

          display: block;
